Witnesses in Marriage: Establishing Ownership, not Obligating Dower
Explains purpose of witnesses in nikah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that witnesses in marriage are for establishing ownership (milk) rather than obligating dower, and apply it to determine the validity of a marriage with non-Muslim witnesses.

Core Idea
Witnesses in nikah prove ownership of the spouse, not the dower — so marriage is valid even without mentioning dower.

This lesson explains a key principle from Uṣūl al-Hidāyah: witnesses in marriage are required to establish the husband's ownership (milk) of the wife's sexual organ (bada'), not to obligate the dower. This principle has a practical application when the witnesses are Dhimmīs and the wife is a Dhimmī. Understanding this will help you see how the Hanafi school prioritizes the essence of the marriage contract over financial terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle and its purpose
Read the Arabic principle: 'إِنَّ الشَّهَادَةَ شُرِطَتْ فِى النِّكَاحَ عَلَى اعْتِبَارَ إِثْبَاتِ الْمِلْكِ لَا عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ وُجُوبِ المَهر'. Understand that witnesses are for proving ownership (milk) of the wife's bada‘, not for obligating the dower. The dower is merely financial, while ownership of the spouse is the core of marriage.
2
Apply to the case of a Muslim man and a Dhimmī woman
Consider a Muslim man marrying a Dhimmī woman in the presence of two Dhimmī witnesses. According to the Shaykhayn (Abū Ḥanīfa and Abū Yūsuf), this marriage is valid. Why? Because witnesses are for proving ownership of the wife's bada‘, which is honorable. The dower being unspecified does not affect validity.
The key is that the witnesses are testifying in favor of the Muslim husband against the Dhimmī wife.
3
Examine the evidence: testimony of Dhimmīs is permissible against a Dhimmī
The reasoning (dalil) is: 'لأن شهادة أهل الذمة على الذمية جائزة' — testimony of Dhimmīs against a Dhimmī is permissible. Since the witnesses testify against the Dhimmī wife (in favor of the Muslim husband), their testimony is accepted, and the marriage is valid.
This is a qiyas: the general rule allows Dhimmī testimony against Dhimmīs, so it applies here.
4
Distinguish the case where both parties are Muslim
If both husband and wife are Muslim, Dhimmī witnesses cannot testify because their testimony would be against a Muslim, which is not permissible. In that case, witnesses must be Muslim.
The principle remains the same: witnesses are for ownership, but the type of witness depends on the parties.

الهداية : كتاب النكاح، ج ۲ ص ۳۲۶، ط: رحمانیه
(5) Indeed, witnessing is required in marriage on the basis of establishing ownership, not on the basis of obligating the dower. Translation: In marriage, witnesses are required on the basis of establishing ownership (milk), not on the basis of making the dower obligatory. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that the condition of witnesses in the chapter of marriage is such that ownership of the wife's sexual organ (bada') is established for the husband, not that the dower becomes obligatory for the husband. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, informs that if a Muslim man marries a Dhimmī woman in the presence of two Dhimmī men, then according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), this marriage will be concluded, because the witnesses required in marriage are for the purpose of establishing the husband's ownership of the wife's sexual organ. Because witnessing is for something that is honorable, and the sexual organ is honorable. There is no honor and greatness in the obligation of wealth. Therefore, if wealth is not mentioned at the time of marriage, the marriage will still be concluded. It is understood that witnessing in marriage is for establishing the husband's ownership of the wife's sexual organ, not for obligating wealth for the husband. Thus, this witnessing is for the husband, against the Dhimmī woman, and the testimony of a disbeliever is accepted in favor of a Muslim, even if it is not accepted against him. Hence, by the testimony of two Dhimmīs, the marriage will be concluded "because the testimony of Dhimmīs against a Dhimmī is permissible." But if the woman is not a Dhimmī, rather she is also a Muslim, then the marriage will not be concluded because that [testimony would be against a Muslim]. = (He is qualified as a muqallid) with fatha on the lam, i.e. a judge or a ruler, and likewise a witness, i.e. similarly a witness because witnessing and judgment are from the same category. (Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 5 p. 15, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah; Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 2 p. 326, Rahmaniyyah)
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage presents a second principle from Uṣūl al-Hidāyah regarding witnesses in marriage: 'Witnesses are required in marriage for establishing ownership, not for obligating the dower.' The author explains that the purpose of witnesses is to prove the husband's ownership (milk) of the wife's sexual organ (bada'), which is considered honorable (muḥtaram). The dower (mahr) is merely financial and does not require such honor. Therefore, if the dower is not mentioned, the marriage remains valid. This principle has a key application: if a Muslim man marries a Dhimmī (protected non-Muslim) woman with two Dhimmī witnesses, the marriage is valid according to the Shaykhayn (Abū Ḥanīfa and Abū Yūsuf). This is because the witnesses are testifying in favor of the Muslim husband against the Dhimmī wife, and the testimony of Dhimmīs against a Dhimmī is permissible. However, if both parties are Muslim, the witnesses must be Muslim because Dhimmi testimony cannot be accepted against a Muslim. The passage also references that witnessing (shahādah) and judgment (qaḍā') are from the same category, reinforcing the interconnectedness of legal functions.

Key Terms
بضع (bada‘): Sexual organ; in marriage context, it refers to the wife's sexual organ over which the husband acquires ownership (milk al-bada‘).
ذمي (dhimmī): A non-Muslim subject of an Islamic state who enjoys protection (dhimmah) and pays jizyah.
الشيخين (al-Shaykhayn): The two shaykhs: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (sometimes including Muhammad al-Shaybani as the third, but here it specifically refers to the two).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of witnesses in marriage according to the principle in this lesson?
A) To make the dower obligatory on the husband
B) To establish the husband's ownership of the wife's sexual organ
C) To ensure both parties are Muslims
D) To prevent fraud in marriage

Key Takeaway
Witnesses in marriage serve to establish the husband's ownership (milk) over the wife's bada‘, not to confirm the dower, and this allows flexibility in the type of witnesses depending on the parties involved.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Witnesses in Nikah: Proving Ownership, Not the Dower
Establishes the purpose of witnesses in nikah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the purpose of witnesses in nikah and explain why non-Muslim witnesses are valid for a non-Muslim woman.

Core Idea
Witnesses in nikah prove the husband's right of intercourse, not the dower.

In Hanafi marriage law, the requirement of witnesses is a key condition. This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes that the purpose of witnesses is to prove the husband's ownership of the right of intercourse (milk al-bud'), not to fix the dower (mahr). This distinction explains why non-Muslim witnesses are accepted when the bride is non-Muslim, as they are testifying against her. Understanding this principle clarifies the underlying reasoning of many nikah rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The author states that witnesses are conditioned for establishing ownership (milk), not for the dower (mahr). This is the core legal maxim.
The Arabic phrase 'عَلَى اعْتِبَارَ إِثْبَاتِ الْمِلْكِ لَا عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ وُجُوبِ المَهر' encapsulates the principle.
2
Examine the proof
The author argues that financial obligations (like mahr) do not require witnesses—sale contracts are valid without them. Therefore, the condition of witnesses must be for something else: the dignity of the right of intercourse.
The Prophet's exception (marrying without witnesses) confirms the general rule.
3
Apply to the dispute
The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) use this principle to validate a marriage with non-Muslim witnesses when the bride is non-Muslim, since the witnesses testify against her.
Imam Muhammad disagrees, but the relied-upon position is that of the two shaykhs.
4
Distinguish cross-madhhab
The Shafi'i school also requires witnesses but views them as a condition for validity; the Hanafi reasoning focuses on the proof of ownership, not the dower.
This leads to practical differences in rulings on who can witness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الشَّهَادَةَ شُرِطَتْ فِى النِّكَاحَ عَلَى اعْتِبَارَ إِثْبَاتِ الْمِلْكِ لَا عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ وُجُوبِ المَهر . لأن شهادة أهل الذمة على الذمية جائزة . وَلَهُمَا أَنَّ الشَّهَادَةَ شُرِطَتْ فِي النِّكَاحِ عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ إِثْبَاتِ الْمِلْكِ لِوُرُودِهِ عَلَى مَحَلِّ ذِي خَطَرٍ لَا عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ وُجُوبِ الْمَهْرِ إِذْ لَا شَهَادَةَ تُشْتَرَطُ فِي لُزُومِ الْمَالِ . الْبَحْرُ الرَّائِقُ : أَنَّ الشَّهَادَةَ شُرِطَتْ فِي النِّكَاحِ عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ إِثْبَاتِ الْمِلْكِ مُطْلَقِ الْمُتْعَةِ لِوُرُودِهِ أَى لِوُرُودِ الْمِلْكِ عَلَى مَحَلِّ ذِي خَطَرٍ فَيُشْتَرَطُ الشَّهَادَةُ تَعْظِيماً لِلْأَبْضَاعِ فَيَكُونُ الرَّجُلُ هُوَ الْمُخَاطَبَ بِالشَّهَادَةِ لِأَجْلِ أَنَّهُ يَمْلِكُ الْبُضْعَ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّهُ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ مَخْصُوصاً بِالنِّكَاحِ بِغَيْرِ شُهُودٍ لَا عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ أَى لَا يُشْتَرَطُ الْإِشْهَادُ عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ وُجُوبِ الْمَهْرِ لَهَا عَلَيْهِ إِذْ لَا شَهَادَةَ تُشْتَرَطُ فِي لُزُومِ الْمَالِ لِأَنَّ إِيجَابَ الْمَالِ يَصِحُّ بِلَا شُهُودٍ كَالْبَيْعِ وَغَيْرِهِ وَهُمَا شَاهِدَانِ عَلَيْهَا أَى الذِّمِّيَّانِ شَاهِدَانِ عَلَيْهَا أَى عَلَى الذِّمِّيَّةِ فَشَهَادَةُ أَهْلِ الذِّمَّةِ عَلَى الذِّمِّيَّةِ جَائِزَةٌ . الْبِنَايَةُ : كِتَابُ النِّكَاحِ ج 5 ص 18 ط دَارِ الْكُتُبِ الْعِلْمِيَّةِ . الْهِدَايَةُ كِتَابُ النِّكَاحِ ج 2 ص 327 ط رَحْمَانِيَّة
Indeed, the condition of witnesses in marriage is for the purpose of establishing ownership, not for the purpose of making the dower obligatory. Because the testimony of the People of the Book against a woman of the People of the Book is permissible. And for them (the two Sahibayn) that the condition of witnesses in marriage is for the purpose of proving ownership because it relates to a matter of great significance, not for the purpose of making the dower obligatory, since no testimony is required for the necessity of wealth. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 'The condition of witnesses in marriage is for the purpose of proving ownership absolutely of the pleasure (right of intercourse) because it (ownership) relates to a matter of great significance, so witnesses are required to dignify the rights of intercourse. Thus, the man is addressed regarding witnesses because he owns the right of intercourse. Do you not see that the Prophet ﷺ was distinguished by marriage without witnesses? Not for the purpose—that is, witnesses are not required for the purpose of making the dower obligatory for her against him, since no testimony is required for the necessity of wealth, because the obligation of wealth is valid without witnesses, like sale and other contracts. And they are two witnesses against her, i.e., the two dhimmis are witnesses against her, i.e., against the dhimmi woman. So the testimony of the People of the Book against a dhimmi woman is permissible.' Al-Binaya: Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 5 p. 18, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 2 p. 327, Rahmaniyyah.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of a key principle in Hanafi marriage law: the requirement of witnesses in a nikah contract is for the purpose of establishing the husband's ownership of the right of intercourse (milk al-bud'), not for fixing the dower (mahr). The author of Al-Hidayah uses this principle to explain a specific ruling: if a Muslim man marries a non-Muslim woman (dhimmi) in the presence of two non-Muslim witnesses, the marriage is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs). The reasoning is that the witnesses are required due to the dignity of the right of intercourse, which is a matter of great significance. Since the dower is a financial obligation that does not require witnesses (like a sale contract), the condition of witnesses must be for something else—the proof of ownership of the right of intercourse. The testimony of non-Muslims is accepted against a non-Muslim woman because they are testifying against her. However, if the woman is Muslim, the testimony of non-Muslims is not accepted against her, so the marriage would not be valid. The passage also includes a reference to the Prophet ﷺ being distinguished by marriage without witnesses, indicating that the requirement of witnesses is not absolute but a recommended precaution for the dignity of the contract.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahāda): Witnesses present at a marriage contract to attest to the agreement.
ملک (milk): Ownership in the context of marriage, specifically the husband's right to the wife's right of intercourse (milk al-bud').
مهر (mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife as an obligation of the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school require witnesses in a marriage contract according to this passage?
A) To make the dower obligatory on the husband
B) To prove the husband's ownership of the right of intercourse
C) To satisfy a requirement that applies to all contracts
D) To comply with the Prophet's specific practice

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires witnesses in nikah to prove the husband's ownership of the right of intercourse, not to fix the dower.

Contract by Agent: The Hanafi Maxim of Legal Attribution
States that a contract performed by an agent is legally equivalent to being performed by the principal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim regarding contracts performed by an agent and apply it to determine the validity of a marriage contract where the principal is present.

Core Idea
The agent's contract is the principal's in law — the principal is the real party.

This lesson examines a foundational maxim in Hanafi mu'amalat: the act of an agent is legally attributed to the principal. The source text from Al-Hidayah expresses this principle concisely and applies it to the context of marriage. Understanding this maxim is essential for grasping how agency operates in Islamic law, particularly in contracts where the principal's presence affects the fulfillment of conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Recognize the two roles: the ma'mur (agent) who physically performs the act, and the amir (principal) who authorizes it.
The agent is the 'one commanded'; the principal is the 'commander'.
2
Distinguish reality from legal effect
Understand that haqiqatan (in reality) the agent acts, but hukman (in legal effect) the act is attributed to the principal.
This duality is crucial for legal consequences.
3
Apply to the nikah scenario
Given a father (principal) instructs an agent to marry his daughter, and only one witness is present besides the father, determine validity using the maxim.
The father counts as a witness because the agent's contract is legally his.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الْعَقْدَ الْوَاقِعَ مِنَ الْمَأْمُورِ حَقِيْقَةً كَالْوَاقِعِ مِنَ الْآمِرِ حُكْمًا
Indeed, the contract that occurs from the one commanded (agent) in reality is like the one occurring from the commander (principal) legally.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage presents a key legal maxim in Hanafi fiqh: the act of an agent (ma'mur) is effectively the act of the principal (amir) in the eyes of the law. The author of Al-Hidayah uses this principle to explain a specific case: if a person commands another to act as his agent in marrying his minor daughter, and the agent performs the marriage in the presence of one witness while the father (the principal) is also present, the marriage is valid. The reasoning is that the contract performed by the agent is legally considered the contract of the principal. Since the principal (father) is present, the requirement of two witnesses is fulfilled: the principal himself and the one witness. The agent is merely a messenger (safir) and the rights of the marriage return to the principal. Thus, the agent's act is attributed to the principal for legal purposes.

Key Terms
مأمور (ma'mur): The person commanded to perform an act; the agent.
آمر (amir): The person who commands; the principal who authorizes the agent.
حقيقةً (haqīqatan): In reality; the actual physical performance of the contract by the agent.
حكمًا (ḥukman): In legal effect; the contract is attributed to the principal for all legal consequences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this principle, if a father instructs an agent to marry his minor daughter, and the agent performs the marriage with only one witness while the father is present, is the marriage valid?
A) No, because an agent's act cannot substitute for the father's presence
B) Yes, because the agent's act is considered the father's act, and the father counts as a witness
C) No, because two witnesses are always required regardless
D) Yes, because the agent himself counts as a witness

Key Takeaway
The agent's contract is the principal's for legal purposes, so the principal bears all rights and obligations.

Nikah — Marriage

8 min
Marriage by Proxy: Agent's Contract Attributed to Principal
Explaining agency principle in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the agent's contract is attributed to the principal in marriage agency and explain why the presence of the father makes the agent count as a witness.

Core Idea
In marriage agency, the agent is a mere messenger; the contract is attributed to the principal, making the agent a witness if the principal is present.

Marriage requires two witnesses. But what if a father sends an agent to contract his minor daughter's marriage and only one additional witness is present? The Hanafi school resolves this through a key principle of agency: the agent's contract is legally considered as if performed by the principal. This lesson unpacks that principle and its application to a specific case.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
The author first lays down the rule: 'A contract by the commissioned agent is legally like a contract by the commander.' Understand that this is the foundational legal maxim for marriage agency.
2
Identify the case
A father orders a man to marry his minor daughter. The agent performs the contract in the presence of one witness while the father is also present. The question: is the marriage valid when only one external witness is available?
Case from al-Hidayah
3
Apply the principle
Because the agent's act is attributed to the principal, the father is deemed the direct contractor (mubashir). The agent is not a party but a messenger (safir). Thus, the agent can serve as a witness, making the total witnesses two: the agent and the one external witness.
Unity of gathering (ittiḥād al-majlis) is required.
4
Derive the ruling
With two witnesses present (the agent and the one external witness), the condition of witnessing is fulfilled. The marriage is valid (sahih).
If father were absent, the agent would be the contractor and only one witness would fail the requirement.
5
Consider the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school does not count the agent as a witness because they require two witnesses from among those present at the contract, not counting the agent who is a party to the contract. Hanafis consider the agent a messenger, hence a valid witness.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Shafi'i, the marriage would be invalid if only one external witness is present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الهداية كتاب النكاح، ج ۲ ص ۳۲۷، ط: رحمانیه

وَمَنْ أَمَرَ رَجُلا أَنْ يُزَوِّجَ ابْنَتَهُ الصَّغِيرَةَ فَزَوَّجَهَا بِحَضْرَةِ رَجُلٍ وَاحِدٍ فَلَا يَخُلُو إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ الْأَبُ حَاضِرًا أَوْ غَائِبًا، فَإِنْ كَانَ حَاضِرًا جَازَ النِّكَاحُ لِأَنَّ الْآبَ يُجْعَلُ مُبَاشِرًا لِلْعَقْدِ وَيَكُونُ الْوَكِيلُ شَاهِدًا لِأَنَّ الْمَجْلِسَ مُتَّحِدٌ ، فَجَازَ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْعَقْدُ الْوَاقِعُ مِنَ الْمَأْمُورِ حَقِيقَةٌ كَالْوَاقِعِ مِنَ الْآمِرِ حُكْمًا لِكَوْنِ الْوَكِيلِ فِي بَابِ النِّكَاحِ (سَفِيرًا وَمُعَبِّرًا.
العناية: كتاب النكاح، ج ۳ ص ۲۰۶، ط: دار الفکر وَمَنْ أَمَرَ رَجُلًا أَنْ يُزَوِّجَ ابْنَتَهُ الصَّغِيرَةَ فَزَوَّجَهَا وَالْأَبُ حَاضِرُ بِشَهَادَةِ رَجُلٍ وَاحِدٍ سِوَاهُمَا جَازَ النِّكَاحُ لِأَنَّ الْابَ يُجْعَلُ مُبَاشِرًا لاتِّحَادِ الْمَجْلِسِ وَيَكُونُ الْوَكِيلُ سَفِيرًا وَمُعَبِّرًا فَيَبْقَى الْمُزَوِّجُ شَاهِدًا.
(2) Indeed, the contract that occurs from the commissioned person in reality is like that which occurs from the commander in terms of ruling. Translation: The contract that the commissioned agent actually performs is like that performed by the commander in legal effect. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that the contract the agent makes is legally attributed to the principal, i.e., the agent's contracting is as if the principal contracts. The author of al-Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, proves that if someone orders another to act as agent and marry his minor daughter, and the agent marries her in the presence of one witness while the father is also present, the marriage is valid because in this case the girl's father is the principal and commander, and the agent is the commissioned person. Since a contract emanating from the commissioned person is legally considered from the commander, here too the direct contractor (i.e., the one performing the marriage contract) is counted as the father. This is because all rights in marriage revert to the principal; the agent is merely a messenger and interpreter. When the father is the contractor, besides the contractor there is a commissioned (agent) and one witness, so there are effectively two witnesses. And for them (the two) that testimony is required in marriage on the basis of establishing ownership because it pertains to a matter of great consequence, not on the basis of the obligation of dower, since no testimony is required for the binding nature of property. al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Book of Marriage, vol. 3 p. 97, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami (that testimony is required in marriage on the basis of establishing ownership of absolute pleasure (because it pertains) i.e., because ownership pertains to a place of great consequence, so testimony is required as a veneration for private parts. Thus the man is addressed with testimony because he owns the private part. Do you not see that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was distinguished in marriage without witnesses. (Not) on the basis i.e., notification is not required on the basis (of the obligation of dower) upon him (since no testimony is required for the binding of property because imposing property is valid without witnesses like sale and other things. (And they are two witnesses against her) i.e., the two dhimmis are witnesses against her, i.e., against the dhimmi woman, so testimony of dhimmis against a dhimmi woman is permissible. al-Binayah: Book of Marriage, vol. 5 p. 18, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah; al-Hidayah, Book of Marriage, vol. 2 p. 327, Rahmaniyyah. They are present, and marriage is concluded in the presence of two witnesses, so here too the marriage will be concluded. And whoever orders a man to marry his minor daughter, and he marries her in the presence of one man, it does not go beyond either that the father is present or absent. If he is present, the marriage is valid because the father is considered the direct contractor of the contract, and the agent becomes a witness because the gathering is unified. So it is permissible that the contract occurring from the commissioned in reality is like that occurring from the commander in ruling, because the agent in the chapter of marriage is a messenger and interpreter. al-'Inayah: Book of Marriage, vol. 3 p. 206, Dar al-Fikr. And whoever orders a man to marry his minor daughter, and he marries her while the father is present with the testimony of one other than them, the marriage is valid because the father is considered the direct contractor due to the unity of the gathering, and the agent becomes a messenger and interpreter, so the one who marries remains a witness.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof from the Hidayah commentary, explaining a principle of marriage agency. The author first states the principle: a contract by a commissioned person (ma'mur) is legally attributed to the commander (amir). He then applies it to a specific case: a father orders an agent to marry his minor daughter. The agent performs the contract in the presence of one witness while the father is also present. The ruling is that the marriage is valid because the father is deemed the direct contractor (mubashir) and the agent becomes a witness, fulfilling the requirement of two witnesses. The proof includes reasoning from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-'Inayah. The key point is that in marriage agency, the agent is merely a messenger (safir) and interpreter (mu'bir); the principal retains all rights. The presence of the father makes the agent count as a witness, so there are the needed two witnesses. The passage also discusses that testimony in marriage is required to establish ownership (milk) of the private part, not for dower, which is a property matter and does not require witnesses. This is a Hanafi position.

Key Terms
مأمور (ma'mūr): The commissioned agent or deputy who performs an act on behalf of the principal.
آمر (amir): The person who gives the order or commission; the principal in an agency relationship.
سفیر (safīr): A messenger or intermediary who merely conveys the contract without having any legal effect as a party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the father is considered the direct contractor and the agent is counted as a witness.
C) Because the presence of the father alone is sufficient for validity.
D) Because the external witness is a Muslim male.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi marriage agency, when the principal is present, the agent's contract is attributed to the principal, allowing the agent to serve as a witness and fulfill the two-witness requirement.

The Principle of Prohibition by Fosterage
Stating the hadith principle on fosterage prohibitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith principle that prohibition by fosterage equals prohibition by lineage and apply it to identify prohibited marriages.

Core Idea
Fosterage creates the same marital prohibitions as blood lineage – a principle from the Prophet's saying.

This lesson anchors a fundamental rule in Islamic family law. The Prophet ﷺ declared that what is prohibited by blood is also prohibited by fosterage. We will examine the hadith, its meaning, and its application to cases like marrying one's foster mother or foster sister. Understanding this principle is key to identifying prohibited relationships in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the Hadith
Learn the Arabic text verbatim: 'يَحْرُمُ مِنَ الرَّضَاعِ مَا يَحْرُمُ مِنَ النَّسَبِ' and its translation.
This hadith is your primary textual anchor.
2
Understand the Analogy
Recognize that fosterage (radāʿah) creates the same marital prohibitions as lineage (nasab). The prohibition is not on the relationship itself but on marriage.
The analogy is comprehensive: every relative prohibited by blood is also prohibited by fosterage.
3
Identify Prohibited Relationships
List those prohibited by lineage (mother, sister, daughter, aunt, etc.) and map them to foster equivalents (foster mother, foster sister, etc.).
Use the standard list of mahram from lineage.
4
Note Conditions of Fosterage
Remember that Hanafi fiqh requires at least two full breastfeedings within the first two years for the prohibition to take effect. A single feeding does not establish fosterage.
This detail is not in the hadith but is based on other texts.
5
Apply to New Cases
Given a hypothetical scenario, determine if marriage is prohibited by applying the principle and the conditions.
Always check if valid fosterage exists first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان المحرمات (۷) إِنَّهُ يَحْرُمُ مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ مَا يَحُرُمُ مِنَ النَّسَبِ. ترجمہ: رضاعت سے وہ رشتے حرام ہوتے ہیں جو نسب کی وجہ سے حرام ہوتے ہیں۔ تشریح مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو رشتے نسب کی وجہ سے حرام ہوتے ہیں وہ رضاعت کی وجہ سے بھی حرام ہوتے ہیں، یہ اصول در حقیقت نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد گرامی ہے: يَحْرُمُ مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ مَا يَحْرُمُ مِنَ النَّسَبِ . صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ رضاعی ماں، رضاعی بہن وغیرہ سے نکاح جائز نہیں ، اس لئے کہ جو رشتے نسب سے حرام ہوتے ہیں رضاعت سے بھی وہ حرام ہوتے ہیں اور چونکہ نسبی ماں ، بہن سے نکاح جائز نہیں تو رضاعی ماں بہن سے بھی نکاح جائز نہیں ۔ الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب النكاح، ج ۲ ص ۳، ط: المطبعة الخيرية الهداية كتاب النكاح، فصل في بيان المحرمات، ج ۲ ص ۳۲۷، ط: رحمانیه مسلم كتاب الرضاع، باب ما يحرم من الرضاعة ما يحرم من الولادة، رقم الحديث: ۱۴۴۵ يَحْرُمُ مِنْ الرَّضَاعِ مَا يَحْرُمُ مِنْ النَّسَبِ وَذَكَرَ عُرْوَةُ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا هَذَا
Section on the explanation of prohibited women. (7) Indeed, what is prohibited from fosterage is what is prohibited from lineage. Translation: From fosterage, those relationships are forbidden which are forbidden from lineage. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that relationships forbidden due to lineage are also forbidden due to fosterage. This principle is in fact the noble saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'What is prohibited from fosterage is what is prohibited from lineage.' The author of al-Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, states that marriage with a foster mother, foster sister, etc., is not permissible because relationships prohibited from lineage are also prohibited from fosterage, and since marriage with a biological mother or sister is not permissible, so too it is not permissible with a foster mother or sister. al-Jawharat al-Nayyirah: Book of Marriage, vol. 2 p. 3, al-Matba'ah al-Khayriyyah; al-Hidayah, Book of Marriage, Section on Prohibited Women, vol. 2 p. 327, Rahmaniyyah; Muslim, Book of Fosterage, Chapter: What is Prohibited from Fosterage is What is Prohibited from Birth, Hadith no. 1445: 'What is prohibited from fosterage is what is prohibited from lineage.' And Urwah narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them both) this.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof directly quoting a hadith. It is a memorization anchor for a key principle in Islamic family law: fosterage (rada'ah) creates the same marital prohibitions as blood lineage (nasab). The author states the principle and then applies it: marrying one's foster mother or foster sister is prohibited. The proof is the hadith from Sahih Muslim. The passage also references standard Hanafi texts like al-Hidayah and al-Jawharat al-Nayyirah. This is a universal principle agreed upon by all schools, but the Hanafi school has detailed conditions for what constitutes fosterage (e.g., two full breastfeedings within the first two years). The text does not delve into those conditions here.

Key Terms
رضاعة (raḍāʿah): Fosterage; the relationship established by breastfeeding a child under specific conditions.
نسب (nasab): Lineage; blood relationship through birth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Marrying your foster sister

D) Marrying your foster father's sister

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'yuhramu min al-rada'ah ma yuhramu min al-nasab' is a foundational principle: fosterage creates the same marital prohibitions as blood lineage.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Married Woman is Legally Considered as Consummated
States a legal principle with immediate application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a married woman is legally considered as consummated and apply it to determine the permissibility of intercourse when combining two sisters.

Core Idea
A married woman is legally considered as consummated — this presumption prevents combining sisters in intercourse.

This lesson introduces a key legal fiction (hukm) from Hanafi fiqh: once a woman becomes a wife, she is treated as if consummated, even if no actual intercourse occurred. This presumption has practical consequences, especially when a man owns a female slave and marries her sister. Understanding this principle helps you navigate the prohibition of combining two sisters in intercourse.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Read the Arabic and English of the principle: 'Verily, the married woman is legally considered as consummated.' Memorize it.
The phrase 'hukman' indicates this is a legal presumption, not a physical fact.
2
Identify the legal consequence
The wife is treated as a consummated woman for rulings where actual consummation would matter.
This affects rules like combining sisters in marriage or intercourse.
3
Apply to the case of a female slave's sister
Consider a man who has a female slave with whom he has had intercourse. He then marries the slave's sister. The marriage is valid, but he cannot have intercourse with either the slave or the new wife.
The wife is mawtu'ah hukman, the slave is actually mawtu'ah. They become like two sisters in his possession.
4
Explain the prohibition of combining sisters
Intercourse with one is prohibited because it would be combining two sisters, which is haram based on Quran 4:23.
The principle extends the prohibition to a case where only one is actually consummated.
5
Identify the exception
The man can make his female slave forbidden to himself (e.g., by selling or gifting her) to permit intercourse with the wife.
Once the slave is no longer his property, the combination is removed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸) إِنَّ الْمَنْكُوحَةَ مَوْطُوعَةٌ حُكْمًا. ترجمہ: منکوحہ حکماً موطوء ہ ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو عورت منکوحہ بن جائے تو یہ حکم کے اعتبار سے موطوء ہ ہوتی ہے یعنی گویا کہ اس کی ساتھ وطی ہو چکی ہے، اب اس پر موطوء ہ کا حکم لاگو ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی موطوء ہ باندی کی بہن سے نکاح کر لیا تو یہ نکاح تو درست ہے کیوں کہ یہ اپنے اہل یعنی عاقل اور بالغ کی طرف سے صادر ہو کر اپنے محل یعنی محل نکاح میں واقع ہوا ہے، اس لئے نکاح تو صحیح ہے لیکن یہ شخص نہ تو مملوکہ باندی سے وطی کر سکتا ہے اور نہ ہی اُس کی منکوحہ بہن سے۔ مملو کہ باندی سے تو وطی اس لئے جائز نہیں کہ منکوحہ اس کی بہن ہے اور وہ حکما موطوء ہ کے درجے میں ہے، اب اگر وہ مملوکہ سے وطی کرے تو جمع بين الأختين وطئاً لازم آ رہا ہے۔ البتہ اگر یہ شخص اپنی مملوکہ باندی کو بیع ، تزویج یا ہبہ مع التسلیم جیسے اسباب میں سے کسی سبب سے اپنے اوپر حرام کر دے تو منکوحہ باندی سے
(8) Verily, the married woman is legally considered as consummated. Translation: The married woman is legally considered as consummated. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that when a woman becomes married, she is in legal consideration considered as if she has been consummated, meaning as if intercourse has occurred with her. Now the ruling of a consummated woman will apply to her. The author of al-Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is explaining that if a person marries the sister of his female slave with whom he has had intercourse, then this marriage is valid because it emanates from someone who is competent (i.e., sane and adult) and occurs in its proper place (i.e., subject of marriage). So the marriage is valid, but this man cannot have intercourse with his owned female slave nor with her married sister. Intercourse with the owned female slave is not permissible because the married woman is her sister and she is legally in the rank of a consummated woman. If he were to have intercourse with the owned female slave, he would be combining between two sisters in terms of intercourse. However, if this man makes his owned female slave forbidden to himself through one of the means such as sale, marriage, or gift with delivery, then [the text cuts off].
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage presents a legal principle (usul) from the Hidayah: a married woman (mankuhah) is legally considered as if she has been consummated (mawtu'ah hukman), even if no actual intercourse has taken place. The Urdu commentary explains that this is a legal presumption: once a woman becomes a wife, she is treated as a consummated woman for certain rulings. The author then applies this to a case: if a man marries the sister of his female slave whom he has previously had intercourse with, the marriage is valid. However, due to this principle, he cannot have intercourse with either the married sister (his new wife) or the original female slave. Why? Because the married woman is legally considered consummated, so she and her sister (the female slave) are now two sisters in a relationship that prohibits simultaneous intercourse (jam' bayn al-ukhtayn). The female slave is already mawtu'ah (consummated) by him, and the new wife is mawtu'ah hukman. Therefore, to have intercourse with the slave would be combining two sisters, which is prohibited. The only way to permit intercourse with the slave is to first make her forbidden to him (e.g., by selling, marrying, or gifting her away), thus severing the slave's status as his property. The passage ends abruptly but completes the ruling: after the slave is forbidden, intercourse with the married sister becomes permissible.

Key Terms
منكوحة (mankuhah): A woman who has entered into a valid marriage contract.
موطوءة حكماً (mawtu'ah hukman): Legally considered as if she has been sexually consummated, even if no actual intercourse has occurred.
جمع بين الأختين (jam' bayn al-ukhtayn): Combining two sisters in marriage or intercourse, which is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can a man not have intercourse with his female slave after marrying the slave's sister?
A) Because the female slave is no longer his property after the marriage.
B) Because the married woman is legally considered consummated, making the slave and wife like two sisters.
C) Because the marriage contract invalidates ownership of the slave.
D) Because the principle applies only if actual consummation occurred.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle 'al-mankuhah mawtu'ah hukman' treats a wife as consummated for rulings, preventing circumvention of the prohibition on combining sisters in intercourse.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
8 min
The Married Woman is Legally Cohabited: Principle and Application
Explanation of a legal principle and its application to a case of marriage and slave ownership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a married woman is legally considered cohabited to cases involving marriage and female slaves, and explain the prohibition of combining two sisters in intercourse.

Core Idea
A married woman is legally treated as cohabited, even if intercourse never occurred, making her sister forbidden for intercourse.

In Hanafi fiqh, marriage creates a legal reality that affects prohibitions. This lesson examines the principle 'al-mankūḥatu mawṭū'atum ḥukman' and its application when a man marries the sister of his female slave. Understanding this legal fiction is essential for correctly applying rulings on permissible and forbidden relationships.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Explain the literal and legal meaning of 'al-mankūḥatu mawṭū'atum ḥukman': a married woman is legally considered cohabited.
This principle is a legal fiction, not a statement about actual fact.
2
Identify the case
The case is a man who has had intercourse with his female slave and then marries the slave's sister.
The slave is mawṭū'a (actually cohabited); the wife is mawṭū'a ḥukman (legally cohabited).
3
Derive the rulings
The marriage is valid because it meets the conditions. However, intercourse with the slave girl is prohibited because the wife is legally cohabited, creating a prohibition of combining two sisters.
The prohibition can be removed if the slave is made forbidden through sale, marriage, or gift.
4
Connect to the dalil
The hadith on breastfeeding (yuharramu bi-al-radaāi mā yuharramu bi-al-wilādah) is cited to show that a legal relationship (like marriage) can create prohibitions analogous to biological relationships.
This is a dalīl naqlī used to support the principle through analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸) إِنَّ الْمَنْكُوحَةَ مَوْطُوعَةٌ حُكْمًا. ترجمہ: منکوحہ حکماً موطوء ہ ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو عورت منکوحہ بن جائے تو یہ حکم کے اعتبار سے موطوء ہ ہوتی ہے یعنی گویا کہ اس کی ساتھ وطی ہو چکی ہے، اب اس پر موطوء ہ کا حکم لاگو ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی موطوء ہ باندی کی بہن سے نکاح کر لیا تو یہ نکاح تو درست ہے کیوں کہ یہ اپنے اہل یعنی عاقل اور بالغ کی طرف سے صادر ہو کر اپنے محل یعنی محل نکاح میں واقع ہوا ہے، اس لئے نکاح تو صحیح ہے لیکن یہ شخص نہ تو مملوکہ باندی سے وطی کر سکتا ہے اور نہ ہی اُس کی منکوحہ بہن سے۔ مملو کہ باندی سے تو وطی اس لئے جائز نہیں کہ منکوحہ اس کی بہن ہے اور وہ حکما موطوء ہ کے درجے میں ہے، اب اگر وہ مملوکہ سے وطی کرے تو جمع بين الأختين وطئاً لازم آ رہا ہے۔ البتہ اگر یہ شخص اپنی مملوکہ باندی کو بیع ، تزویج یا ہبہ مع التسلیم جیسے اسباب میں سے کسی سبب سے اپنے اوپر حرام کر دے تو منکوحہ باندی سے وطی کر سکتا ہے اس لئے کہ مانع زائل ہو گیا۔ الْحَدِيث قَالَ: يَحْرُمُ بِالرَّضَاعِ مَا يَحْرُمُ بِالْوِلَادَةِ، وَفِيهِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى أَنَّ الرَّضَاعَ مِنْ أَسْبَابِ التَّحْرِيمِ، وَأَنَّهُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ النَّسَبِ فِى ثُبُوتِ الْحُرْمَةِ، لِأَنَّ ثُبُوتَ الْحُرُمَةِ بِالنَّسَبِ لِحَقِيقَةِ الْبَعْضِيَّةِ أَوْ شُبْهَةِ الْبَعْضِيَّةِ، وَفِى الرَّضَاعِ شُبُهَةُ الْبَعْضِيَّةِ بِمَا يَحْصُلُ بِاللَّبَنِ الَّذِي هُوَ جُزْء الْآدَمِيَّةِ فِي إِنْبَاتِ اللَّحْمِ وَإِنْشَازِ الْعَظْمِ وَإِلَيْهِ أَشَارَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ: الرَّضَاعُ مَا أَنبَتَ اللَّحْمَ وَأَنْشَرَ الْعَظْمَ وَفِيهِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى أَنَّ الْحُرُمَةَ بِالرَّضَاعِ كَمَا تَثْبُتُ مِنْ جَانِبِ الْأُمَّهَاتِ تَثْبُتُ مِنْ جَانِبِ الْآبَاءِ وَهُوَ الزَّوْجُ الَّذِى نَزَلَ لَبَنُهَا بِوَطْئِهِ، فَإِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ شَبَّهَهُ بِالنَّسَبِ فِي التَّحْرِيم وَالْحُرِّمَةُ بِالنَّسَبِ تَثْبُتُ مِنْ الْجَانِبَيْنِ فَكَذَلِكَ بِالرَّضَاعَ. المبسوط للسرخسی کتاب الرضاع ج ۵ ص ۱۳۳، ط: دار المعرفة بَحْرُمُ مِنَ الرَّضَاعِ مَا يَحْرُمُ مِنَ النَّسَبِ وَمَعْنَاهُ أَنَّ الْحُرْمَةَ بِسَبَبِ الرَّضَاعِ تُعْتَبَرُ بِحُرْمَةِ النَّسَبِ فَشَمِلَ حَلِيلَةَ الِابْنِ، وَالْآبِ مِنْ الرَّضَاعِ لِأَنَّهَا حَرَامٌ بِسَبَبِ النَّسَبِ فَكَذَا بِسَبَبِ الرَّضَاعِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَكْثَرِ أَهْلِ الْعِلْمِ كَذَا فِي الْمَبْسُوطِ. البحر الرائق: كتاب الرضاع، ج ۳ ص ۸ ۲۳۸، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي الهداية: كتاب النكاح، فصل في بيان المحرمات، ج ۲ ص ۳۲۸، ط: رحمانیه
Indeed the married woman is legally cohabited. Translation: A married woman is legally cohabited. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that a woman who becomes married is, by legal ruling, considered as cohabited, meaning as if intercourse has occurred with her, so the ruling of a cohabited woman applies to her. The author of al-Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is explaining that if a person marries the sister of his female slave with whom he has had intercourse, then this marriage is valid because it is issued from its proper agent (a sane and adult person) and directed to its proper place (marriage), so the marriage is valid. However, this person can neither have intercourse with the owned slave girl nor with her married sister. Intercourse with the owned slave girl is not permissible because the married woman is her sister and she is legally in the status of a cohabited woman; if he has intercourse with the owned slave girl, then combining two sisters through intercourse would occur. But if this person makes his owned slave girl forbidden to himself by one of the means such as sale, marriage, or gift with delivery, then he may have intercourse with the married slave girl because the impediment has been removed. The hadith said: 'What is prohibited due to lineage is prohibited due to breastfeeding.' In it is evidence that breastfeeding is a cause of prohibition and that it is like lineage in establishing prohibition, because the establishment of prohibition through lineage is due to actual partiality or semblance of partiality, and in breastfeeding there is a semblance of partiality through the milk which is a part of the human being in growing flesh and strengthening bones. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) referred to this when he said: 'Breastfeeding is what grows flesh and strengthens bones.' In it is evidence that the prohibition due to breastfeeding is established from the side of mothers as it is established from the side of fathers, i.e., the husband whose intercourse caused her milk. Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) likened it to lineage in prohibition, and prohibition due to lineage is established from both sides, so similarly through breastfeeding. Al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi, Kitab al-Rada', vol. 5 p. 133, Dar al-Ma'rifah. 'What is prohibited due to breastfeeding is what is prohibited due to lineage.' Its meaning is that the prohibition due to breastfeeding is considered in analogy with the prohibition due to lineage, so it includes the wife of the son and the father from breastfeeding, because she is forbidden due to lineage, so likewise due to breastfeeding. This is the view of most scholars. As quoted in al-Mabsut. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Kitab al-Rada', vol. 3 p. 8238, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Nikah, chapter on the statement of prohibitions, vol. 2 p. 328, Rahmaniyyah.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi usul al-fiqh work. The principle 'The married woman is considered cohabited in legal ruling' is explained in the context of marrying the sister of one's female slave. The author of al-Hidayah uses this principle to show that even though the marriage to the sister is valid, the husband cannot have intercourse with the slave girl because the sister (the wife) is legally considered as if she has been cohabited, thus creating a prohibition of combining two sisters through intercourse. The prohibition is lifted only if the slave girl is made forbidden through sale, marriage, or gift. The passage then provides a dalil (proof) from the hadith about breastfeeding, which establishes that breastfeeding creates a prohibition similar to lineage. This analogy is used to support the principle that a married woman is treated as cohabited. The Hanafi school relies on this principle to maintain the prohibition of intercourse with the slave girl while married to her sister.

Key Terms
منکوحة (mankūḥa): A woman who is married (entered into a valid marriage contract).
موطوء (mawṭū'): A woman with whom intercourse has taken place, either actually or legally (ḥukman).
حكماً (ḥukman): By legal ruling, as a matter of legal consideration rather than actual occurrence.
جمع بين الأختين (jam' bayn al-ukhtayn): The prohibition of simultaneously having intercourse with two sisters, whether through marriage or ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'Inna al-mankūḥata mawṭū'atum ḥukman', what is the ruling if a man marries the sister of his female slave with whom he has had intercourse?
A) The marriage is invalid and both women become forbidden.
B) The marriage is valid but he cannot have intercourse with either woman until he divorces the married sister.
C) The marriage is valid, but he cannot have intercourse with the slave girl until he makes her forbidden through sale, marriage, or gift.
D) He may have intercourse with both because marriage does not affect the status of the slave.

Key Takeaway
A married woman is legally considered cohabited, which prohibits intercourse with her sister, but the marriage itself is valid.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Benefiting from One's Own Part is Prohibited: Muṣāhara after Zina and Combining Two Sisters
Ruling with proof: explanation of a principle and its application, with dalīl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle 'istimtā' bi al-juz' ḥarām' and apply it to determine prohibited marriages due to muṣāhara after zina, and to derive the ruling on combining two sisters in marriage or ownership.

Core Idea
Zina creates a partial muṣāhara, making ascendants/descendants of the partner like one's own part — marriage to them is ḥarām.

This lesson examines a foundational Hanafi legal principle: benefiting from one's own body part is prohibited, and how it extends to relatives by affinity after zina. The passage from al-Hidayah and al-Ikhtiyar also addresses the prohibition of combining two sisters, clarifying that mere ownership is permitted but intercourse is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Locate the principle 'Inna al-istimtā'a bi al-juz'i ḥarām' in the text. Understand that this principle means a person cannot derive benefit (especially sexual enjoyment) from anyone considered a part of themselves.
The principle is used to explain prohibitions of marriage due to muṣāhara.
2
Apply the Principle to Muṣāhara after Zina
The text states that if a person commits zina with another, a kind of partiality (juz'iyyah) is established. Consequently, the ascendants and descendants of the partner become like one's own parts, making marriage to them prohibited.
This is unique to Hanafi fiqh; some other schools do not extend muṣāhara to zina.
3
Identify the Four Categories of Prohibited Relatives
From the principle, four categories become prohibited: for the man, the mother and daughter of the woman with whom he committed zina; for the woman, the father and son of the man.
These are analogous to the prohibitions of marriage to ascendants and descendants by blood.
4
Examine the Proof for Combining Two Sisters
The text cites Quran 4:23 and a Hadith to prohibit combining two sisters in marriage or intercourse through ownership. The key point: the prohibition applies to intercourse, not to mere ownership of two sisters as slaves.
The consensus is that the text prohibits intercourse, not ownership.
5
Distinguish Between Valid Marriage and Prohibited Intercourse
If a man owns a female slave with whom he has had intercourse, he may marry her sister, but he cannot have intercourse with both. He must either make the slave forbidden or divorce the wife before intercourse.
The ruling shows a practical application of the prohibition.

(۹) إِنَّ الاِسْتِمْتَاعَ بِالْجُزءِ حَرَامٌ . ترجمہ: اپنے جزء سے فائدہ اٹھانا حرام ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ انسان کا اپنے اجزاء میں سے کسی جزء سے فائدہ حاصل کرنا حرام ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ حرمت مصاہرہ سے چار قسم کے رشتے حرام ہو جاتے ہیں، یعنی اگر کسی شخص نے کسی عورت سے زنا کیا تو اب واطی پر موطوء ہعورت کی ماں اور بیٹی حرام ہیں، اور مزنیہ عورت پر واطی زانی کا باپ اور بیٹا حرام ہے، مذکورہ اشخاص سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ ولی یہ ولد کے واسطے سے جزئیت کا سبب ہے یعنی مرد اور عورت میں جزئیت اور بعضیت پیدا کرتا ہے، گویا کہ مرد کا قبیلہ عورت کا قبیلہ ہے اور عورت کا قبیلہ مرد کا قبیلہ ہے اور یہ مزنیہ عورت اس کی جزء بن گئی ، اسی طرح اس عورت کے اصول یعنی ماں دادی و غیر ہ اور فروع یعنی بیٹی پوتی وغیرہ مرد کے جزء بن گئے ہیں، اب اگر واطی موطوء ہ کی بیٹی یا ماں سے نکاح کرے گا تو استمتاع بالجزء یعنی جزء سے فائدہ اٹھانا لازم آئے گا اور جزء سے فائدہ اٹھانا حرام وَلَا يَجُوزُ الْجَمْعُ بَيْنَ الْأُخْتَيْنِ نِكَاحًا، وَلَا بِمِلْكِ يَمِينِ وَطْئًا؛ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: (وَأَنْ تَجْمَعُوا بَيْنَ الْأُخْتَيْنِ إِلَّا مَا قَدْ سَلَفَ وَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ : مَنْ كَانَ يُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ فَلَا يَجْمَعَنَّ مَاءَهُ فِي رَحِمٍ أُخْتَيْنِ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَجْمَعَ بَيْنَهُمَا فِي الْمِلْكِ دُونَ الْوَطْءِ، لِأَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِالنَّصَّ حَرْمَةُ الْوَطْء إِجْمَاعًا. فَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُ أَمَةٌ قَدْ وَطِئَهَا، فَتَزَوَّجَ أُخْتَهَا جَازَ النِّكَاحُ؛ لِصُدُورِهِ مِنْ أَهْلِهِ وَإِضَافَتِهِ إِلَى مَحَلِّهِ. وَلَا يَطَأُ الْأمَةَ؛ لأنَّ لِمَنْكُوحَةَ مَوْطُوءةٌ حُكْمًا، وَلَا يَطَأُ الْمَنْكُوحَةَ حَتَّى يُحَرِّمَ الْامَةَ عَلَيْهِ، فَإِذَا حَرَّمَهَا وَطِءَ الْمَنْكُوحَةَ. وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ وَطِءَ الْمَمْلُوكَةَ وَطِءَ الْمَنْكُوحَةَ، وَحُرِّمَتِ الْمَمْلُوكَةُ حَتَّى يُفَارِقَ الْمَنْكُوحَةَ. الاختيار لتـعـلـيـل الـمـخـتـار : كتاب النكاح، فصل في محرمات النكاح، ج ۳ ص ۸۶، ، ط: مطبعة المجلس القاهرة الهداية كتاب النكاح، ج ۲ ص ۳۲۹، ط: رحمانیه
Indeed, deriving benefit from a part (of oneself) is prohibited. Translation: Benefiting from one's own part is prohibited. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that a person deriving benefit from any of his parts is prohibited. The author of al-Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is explaining that from the prohibition of muṣāhara (affinity), four types of relationships become prohibited: that is, if a person commits zina with a woman, then for the man (the fornicator), the mother and daughter of the woman with whom he committed zina are prohibited, and for the woman (the adulteress), the father and son of the man (the fornicator) are prohibited. Marriage to these persons is not permissible because the relationship of guardianship (walī) causes partiality (juz'iyyah) through the child, meaning it creates partiality and 'some' relationship between the man and woman, as if the man's clan is the woman's clan and the woman's clan is the man's clan. And this adulteress has become his part. Similarly, her ascendants (mothers, grandmothers, etc.) and descendants (daughters, granddaughters, etc.) have become parts of the man. Now, if the man (the fornicator) marries the daughter or mother of the woman with whom he committed zina, then deriving benefit from a part (istimtā' bi al-juz') would become necessary, and deriving benefit from a part is prohibited. And it is not permissible to combine two sisters in marriage, nor to have intercourse with two sisters through ownership (milk yamīn), due to the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And that you combine between two sisters except what has already passed' (Quran 4:23), and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day, let him not combine his water in the wombs of two sisters.' And it is permissible to own both without intercourse, because the intent of the text is the prohibition of intercourse, by consensus. So if a man has a female slave with whom he has had intercourse, and then he marries her sister, the marriage is valid because it issues from its proper agent and is directed to its proper place. And he does not have intercourse with the slave girl because the married sister is legally considered cohabited. And he does not have intercourse with the married woman until he makes the slave girl forbidden to himself. So when he makes her forbidden, he may have intercourse with the married woman. And if he has not had intercourse with the female slave, he may have intercourse with the married woman, and the female slave becomes forbidden until he separates from the married woman. Al-Ikhtiyar li Ta'lil al-Mukhtar: Kitab al-Nikah, chapter on the prohibitions of marriage, vol. 3 p. 86, Maktab al-Majlis al-Qahira. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 2 p. 329, Rahmaniyyah.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi usul. The principle 'Deriving benefit from one's own part is prohibited' is applied to the prohibition of marriage due to muṣāhara (affinity) after zina. The commentary explains that through zina, a kind of partiality (juz'iyyah) is established between the fornicator and the adulteress, extending to her ascendants and descendants. Thus, marrying them would involve deriving benefit from one's own part, which is prohibited. The passage then provides proofs from the Quran and Sunnah regarding the prohibition of combining two sisters in marriage or intercourse through ownership. It reiterates the ruling that if a man marries the sister of his female slave whom he has cohabited, the marriage is valid but intercourse with both is prohibited until the slave is made forbidden. This principle is fundamental in Hanafi fiqh for understanding the prohibitions of affinity based on zina.

Key Terms
استمتاع (istimtā'): Deriving pleasure or benefit, specifically sexual enjoyment.
جزء (juz'): A part or component; here referring to one's own body part or someone considered as such due to muṣāhara/zina.
حرمت مصاہره (ḥurmat muṣāhara): The prohibition of marriage due to affinity (muṣāhara), which includes relationships created by marriage or zina.
جمع بين الأختين (jam' bayn al-ukhtayn): Prohibition of combining two sisters in marriage or intercourse under ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'Inna al-istimtā'a bi al-juz'i ḥarām', which of the following becomes prohibited due to zina?
A) The fornicator may marry the sister of the adulteress.
B) The fornicator may marry the mother or daughter of the adulteress.
C) The fornicator may marry the daughter of the adulteress only if she is not his own child.
D) The fornicator may marry any relative of the adulteress except her mother.

Key Takeaway
The principle 'istimtā' bi al-juz' ḥarām' underlies the Hanafi prohibition of marrying relatives by affinity after zina, and the prohibition of combining two sisters in intercourse.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
The Principle of Prohibition of Benefiting from One's Own Part
Defines a general principle and applies it to specific cases of zina and combining sisters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle 'istimta' bil-juz' haram' and apply it to derive the kinship prohibitions resulting from zina.

Core Idea
Benefiting from one's own part is prohibited — zina creates partiality, making the woman and her ascendants/descendants parts of the man.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi legal principle: benefiting from one's own part is prohibited (istimta' bil-juz' haram). The principle is used to extend marriage prohibitions (hurmah al-musaharah) beyond valid marriage to cases of zina. By understanding how partiality (juz'iyyah) is established through a potential child, you will see why the Hanafi school prohibits marriage to the mother or daughter of a woman with whom one has committed zina.

Guided Path
1
State the principle and its textual basis
Identify the exact phrasing of the principle from the source: 'Indeed, benefiting from one's own part is prohibited.' Note that this is a general rule stated in al-Hidayah.
The principle is not directly from Quran or Hadith but derived by the Hanafi school as a juridical principle.
2
Define key terms: istimta', juz', juz'iyyah
Break down the components: istimta' (benefiting/enjoyment), juz' (part), juz'iyyah (partiality). Understand how these relate to the creation of marital prohibitions through zina.
Partiality (juz'iyyah) is established via a potential child (walad) from the illicit union.
3
Apply the principle to zina: identify the prohibited relations
Following the source, list the four prohibited relations: for the man, the mother and daughter of the woman; for the woman, the father and son of the man. Trace the reasoning: the woman becomes a part of the man, and her ancestors and descendants also become his parts.
The prohibition arises because marriage to these persons would involve benefiting from one's own part.
4
Distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i view
Note that Shafi'is do not consider zina as creating any permanent marriage prohibitions. Their basis is that zina does not establish kinship (musaharah) because it is not a valid contract. The Hanafi view is based on the principle of juz'iyyah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (difference of opinion) with practical consequences.
5
Examine the ancillary rule about combining two sisters
The source also discusses combining two sisters in marriage or ownership. Understand the ruling: one can own two sisters but cannot have intercourse with both simultaneously; if he marries one after having intercourse with the other, he must cease intercourse with the slave girl.
This part demonstrates the principle's application beyond zina, to the prohibition of combining sisters.

(۹) إِنَّ الاِسْتِمْتَاعَ بِالْجُزءِ حَرَامٌ . ترجمہ: اپنے جزء سے فائدہ اٹھانا حرام ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ انسان کا اپنے اجزاء میں سے کسی جزء سے فائدہ حاصل کرنا حرام ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ حرمت مصاہرہ سے چار قسم کے رشتے حرام ہو جاتے ہیں، یعنی اگر کسی شخص نے کسی عورت سے زنا کیا تو اب واطی پر موطوء ہعورت کی ماں اور بیٹی حرام ہیں، اور مزنیہ عورت پر واطی زانی کا باپ اور بیٹا حرام ہے، مذکورہ اشخاص سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ ولی یہ ولد کے واسطے سے جزئیت کا سبب ہے یعنی مرد اور عورت میں جزئیت اور بعضیت پیدا کرتا ہے، گویا کہ مرد کا قبیلہ عورت کا قبیلہ ہے اور عورت کا قبیلہ مرد کا قبیلہ ہے اور یہ مزنیہ عورت اس کی جزء بن گئی ، اسی طرح اس عورت کے اصول یعنی ماں دادی و غیر ہ اور فروع یعنی بیٹی پوتی وغیرہ مرد کے جزء بن گئے ہیں، اب اگر واطی موطوء ہ کی بیٹی یا ماں سے نکاح کرے گا تو استمتاع بالجزء یعنی جزء سے فائدہ اٹھانا لازم آئے گا اور جزء سے فائدہ اٹھانا حرام وَلَا يَجُوزُ الْجَمْعُ بَيْنَ الْأُخْتَيْنِ نِكَاحًا، وَلَا بِمِلْكِ يَمِينِ وَطْئًا؛ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: (وَأَنْ تَجْمَعُوا بَيْنَ الْأُخْتَيْنِ إِلَّا مَا قَدْ سَلَفَ وَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ : مَنْ كَانَ يُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ فَلَا يَجْمَعَنَّ مَاءَهُ فِي رَحِمٍ أُخْتَيْنِ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَجْمَعَ بَيْنَهُمَا فِي الْمِلْكِ دُونَ الْوَطْءِ، لِأَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِالنَّصَّ حَرْمَةُ الْوَطْء إِجْمَاعًا. فَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُ أَمَةٌ قَدْ وَطِئَهَا، فَتَزَوَّجَ أُخْتَهَا جَازَ النِّكَاحُ؛ لِصُدُورِهِ مِنْ أَهْلِهِ وَإِضَافَتِهِ إِلَى مَحَلِّهِ. وَلَا يَطَأُ الْأمَةَ؛ لأنَّ لِمَنْكُوحَةَ مَوْطُوءةٌ حُكْمًا، وَلَا يَطَأُ الْمَنْكُوحَةَ حَتَّى يُحَرِّمَ الْامَةَ عَلَيْهِ، فَإِذَا حَرَّمَهَا وَطِءَ الْمَنْكُوحَةَ. وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ وَطِءَ الْمَمْلُوكَةَ وَطِءَ الْمَنْكُوحَةَ، وَحُرِّمَتِ الْمَمْلُوكَةُ حَتَّى يُفَارِقَ الْمَنْكُوحَةَ. الاختيار لتـعـلـيـل الـمـخـتـار : كتاب النكاح، فصل في محرمات النكاح، ج ۳ ص ۸۶، ، ط: مطبعة المجلس القاهرة الهداية كتاب النكاح، ج ۲ ص ۳۲۹، ط: رحمانیه
ہے، لہذ اواطی کے لئے موطوء ہ کی ماں اور بیٹی سے نکاح حرام ہوگا۔
(9) Indeed, benefiting from one's own part is prohibited. Translation: Benefiting from one's own part is prohibited. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that a person benefiting from any of his own parts is prohibited. The author of al-Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, explains that from the prohibition of kinship (hurmah al-musaharah), four types of relations become prohibited. That is, if a person commits zina with a woman, then for the man, the mother and daughter of the woman with whom he committed zina are prohibited, and for the woman with whom zina was committed, the father and son of the man are prohibited. Marriage to these persons is not permissible because the walad (child) is the cause of partiality (juz'iyyah) through the medium of the child, meaning it creates partiality and belonging between the man and woman. So the man's family becomes the woman's family and the woman's family becomes the man's family, and this woman becomes a part of him. Similarly, her ascendants (principles) like mother, grandmother, etc., and descendants (branches) like daughter, granddaughter, etc., become parts of the man. Now if the man marries the daughter or mother of the woman, benefiting from the part (istimta' bil-juz') becomes necessary, and benefiting from a part is prohibited. And it is not permissible to combine two sisters in marriage, nor through right hand possession (milkyameen) for intercourse, due to His saying: 'And that you combine between two sisters except what has passed' and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not combine his water in the womb of two sisters.' And it is permissible to combine them in ownership without intercourse because the intended meaning of the text is the prohibition of intercourse by consensus. If he has a slave girl whom he has had intercourse with, then he marries her sister, the marriage is valid because it is issued from its proper place and attributed to its proper place. And he does not have intercourse with the slave girl because the married woman is considered as one who has been had intercourse with in terms of ruling. And he does not have intercourse with the married woman until he makes the slave girl prohibited upon himself. So when he makes her prohibited, he can have intercourse with the married one. And if he has not had intercourse with the slave girl, he can have intercourse with the married one, and the slave girl becomes prohibited until he separates from the married one. Al-Ikhtiyar li Ta'lil al-Mukhtar: Kitab al-Nikah, Fasl fi Muharramat al-Nikah, vol. 3, p. 86, Cairo: Majlis Press. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 2, p. 329, Rahmaniyyah. Then, therefore, for the man, marriage to the mother and daughter of the woman with whom he committed zina becomes prohibited.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage defines and applies the principle 'Benefiting from one's own part is prohibited.' The author explains that the principle is used to derive rulings of kinship prohibitions (hurmah al-musaharah) resulting from zina. When a man commits zina with a woman, a relationship of partiality (juz'iyyah) is established through the potential child, making the woman and her relatives (ascendants and descendants) parts of the man. Thus, marrying them would involve benefiting from one's own part, which is prohibited. The text also includes a related rule about combining two sisters in marriage or ownership, citing Quran and Hadith. The Hanafi ruling is that one can own two sisters but cannot have intercourse with both; if he marries one sister after having intercourse with the other, the marriage is valid but he must stop intercourse with the slave girl first.

Key Terms
استمتاع بالجزء (istimta' bil-juz'): Benefiting from one's own part; using a body part or related person for one's own pleasure.
جزئیت (juz'iyyah): The relationship of being a part or partiality, established through parent-child connection.
حرمت مصاہرہ (hurmah al-musaharah): Marriage prohibitions arising from kinship (in-law relations).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle 'istimta' bil-juz' haram', why is it prohibited for a man to marry the mother of a woman he committed zina with?
A) Because the mother is a mahram by blood.
B) Because the woman becomes a part of him, making her mother also his part.
C) Because zina is a sin and cannot create any halal relationship.
D) Because the woman is already married to him.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the principle 'istimta' bil-juz' haram' to derive marriage prohibitions from zina, based on the concept of partiality through a potential child.

Nikah — Marriage

The Principle that Being Owned Contraindicates Being an Owner
Establishes the qawida that mamlukiyya contradicts malikiyya, applied to marriage prohibitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that mamlukiyya contradicts malikiyya and apply it to determine the validity of marriages involving slaves.

Core Idea
Being owned and being an owner cannot coexist in one person; thus a master cannot marry his slave.

This passage establishes a foundational legal maxim in Hanafi fiqh: the status of being owned (mamlukiyya) is inherently contradictory to the status of being an owner (malikiyya). The principle is applied to marriage prohibitions, where a master cannot marry his slave woman nor can a slave marry his mistress, because such a marriage would require the same person to be both owned and an owner. The text then extends this reasoning through analogical deduction to other cases of affinity, such as the mother of one's wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Locate the statement 'إِنَّ الْمَمْلُوكِيَّةَ تُنَافِى الْمَالِكِيَّةَ' and understand its literal meaning: being owned contradicts being an owner.
This is a qawida (maxim) that serves as a foundational rule.
2
Recognize the contradiction
Grasp that one person cannot simultaneously be both a slave (owned) and a master (owner) in relation to the same thing. The attributes are mutually exclusive.
The contradiction is logical and legal; it prevents certain relationships.
3
Apply to master-slave marriage
Consider the case of a master marrying his own slave woman or a slave marrying his mistress. Such a marriage would make the same individual both owner and owned, violating the principle.
The marriage is therefore invalid (batil) from the start.
4
Extend via qiyas to analogous cases
The author uses qiyas to extend the prohibition from the father's intercourse with a woman (creating affinity) to similar cases like the son's intercourse or the mother of one's wife. The 'illa is that intercourse creates a partiality through the child, making enjoyment of that child's ascendants/descendants forbidden.
This shows how a single principle can govern multiple scenarios through analogy.
5
Note the precautionary extension
The text states that even touching and looking are placed in the position of intercourse as a precaution (ihtiyat) to protect the prohibition.
This reflects the Hanafi tendency to guard prohibitions by blocking means leading to them.

Source Text

( ١٠ ) إِنَّ الْمَمْلُوكِيَّةَ تُنَافِى الْمَالِكِيَّةَ .
ترجمہ مملوک ہونا مالک ہونے کے منافی ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مملوک ہونا اور مالک ہونا دو متضاد چیزیں ہیں،ایک شخص مملوک اور مالک نہیں ہوسکتا، کیونکہ جو مالک ہوگا وہ مملوک نہیں ہوسکتا اور جو مملوک ہوگا وہ
مالک نہیں ہوسکتا، لہذ اشخص واحد بیک وقت دو متضاد صفات سے متصف نہیں ہوسکتا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے اس بات کو بتلا رہے ہیں کہ آقا اپنی باندی سے اور غلام اپنی مالکہ سے نکاح نہیں کر سکتا، اس لئے باندی اور غلام مملوک ہیں ، اب اگر باندی بیوی بن جائے اور غلام اپنی مالکہ کا شوہر بن جائے تو مالک بن جائیں جبکہ مملوکیت مالکیت کی منافی ہے، لہذ اشخص واحد کا مملوک ہونا اور مالک ہونا لازم آئے گا اور شخص واحد کا مملوک اور مالک ہونا جائز نہیں ہے، لہذا وَإِذَا ثَبَتَ هَذَا الْحُكْمُ فِي مَوْطُوءَةِ الْآبِ ثَبَتَ فِي مَوْطُوءَةِ الِابْنِ، وَفِي وَطْء أُمِّ امْرَأَتِهِ، وَسَائِرِ مَا يَثْبُتُ بِحُرُمَةِ الْمُصَاهَرَةِ بِالنِّكَاحِ، لِأَنَّ أَحَدًا لَمْ يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَهُمَا وَلِأَنَّ الْوَطْء سَبَبٌ لِلْجُزْئِيَّةِ بِوَاسِطَةِ الْوَلَدِ، وَلِهَذَا يُضَافُ إِلَيْهَا كَمَا يُضَافُ إِلَيْهِ، وَالِاسْتِمْتَاعُ بِالْجُزْءِ حَرَامٌ. وَالْمَسُّ وَالنَّظَرُ دَاعِ إِلَى الْوَطْءِ، فَيُقَامُ مَقَامَهُ احْتِيَاطًا لِلْحُرْمَةِ. الاختيار لتعليل المختار : كتاب النكاح، فصل محرمات النكاح، ج ۳ ص ۸۸، ط: مطبعة المجلس القاهرة
Therefore, for the purpose of intercourse, marriage to the mother and daughter of the woman with whom intercourse occurred becomes forbidden. (10) Indeed, being owned contradicts being an owner. Translation: Being owned is contrary to being an owner. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that being owned and being an owner are two contradictory things; one person cannot be both owned and an owner, because whoever is an owner cannot be owned, and whoever is owned cannot be an owner. Therefore, a single person cannot be described with two contradictory attributes at the same time. The author of al-Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is conveying that a master cannot marry his slave woman, and a slave cannot marry his mistress, because the slave woman and the slave are owned. Now if the slave woman becomes a wife and the slave becomes the husband of his mistress, they would become owners, while being owned contradicts being an owner. Hence, a single person would necessarily be both owned and an owner, and it is not permissible for a single person to be both owned and an owner. Therefore, when this ruling is established concerning the woman with whom the father has had intercourse, it is also established concerning the woman with whom the son has had intercourse, and concerning intercourse with the mother of his wife, and all other cases that establish prohibition through affinity by marriage, because no one has made a distinction between them, and because intercourse is a cause of partiality (part-ownership) through the child, and for this reason the child is attributed to her just as it is attributed to him, and enjoyment of a part is forbidden. And touching and looking lead to intercourse, so they are placed in its position as a precaution for the prohibition. (From al-Ikhtiyar li Ta'lil al-Mukhtar).
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational legal principle (qawida) in Hanafi fiqh: that the status of being owned (mamlukiyya) is inherently contradictory to the status of being an owner (malikiyya). The author explains that a single individual cannot simultaneously be both a slave and a master. The practical application of this principle is in marriage: a master cannot marry his own slave woman, nor can a slave marry his mistress, because such a marriage would necessitate that the same person be both owned and an owner at the same time. For example, if a free man marries his slave, she gains the right to maintenance and other spousal benefits, making her a partial owner of his rights, while she remains his property—a contradiction. The passage then extends the ruling: the prohibition that arises from intercourse (such as that which creates affinity) applies not only to direct cases but also to analogous situations, such as the mother of one's wife or the daughter of one's stepchild. The reasoning is that intercourse is a cause of 'partiality' (juz'iyya) through the child, and since enjoyment of one's own child is forbidden, any means leading to it (lustful touch, gaze) are also prohibited as a precautionary measure. This is a typical Hanafi approach: establishing a core principle and then applying it through analogical reasoning (qiyas) with a strong precautionary element.

Key Terms
مملوکیت (mamlukiyya): The state of being owned as a slave; the legal status of being the property of another.
مالکیت (malikiyya): The state of being an owner; full legal capacity to own and dispose of property and rights.
موطوءة (mawtu'a): A woman with whom one has had sexual intercourse, whether lawful or unlawful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'mamlukiyya contradicts malikiyya', which of the following marriages is invalid?
A) A free man marrying a free woman
B) A master marrying his own slave woman
C) A man marrying his son's ex-wife
D) A man marrying his cousin

Key Takeaway
The principle that being owned contradicts being an owner prohibits a master from marrying his slave woman and a slave from marrying his mistress.
